# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# Prometheus WAL Write-Ahead Log Segment Management

## Your Task

Find all Go source files in prometheus/prometheus that implement the TSDB write-ahead log (WAL): the WAL segment creation and rotation, the WAL record encoding (series, samples, tombstones), the WAL repair on corrupt segments, and the checkpoint creation to truncate old WAL data.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the org domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
*(none — all repos available locally)*

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{

  ],

    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've successfully completed the task. I've identified all Go source files in the prometheus/prometheus repository that implement the TSDB write-ahead log (WAL) functionality and created a comprehensive answer.json file.

## Summary of Findings

The WAL implementation spans across multiple files organized in the `tsdb/wlog` package and related modules:

### Core WAL Files:
- **tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** - Main WAL implementation with segment creation/rotation, writing, and repair
- **tsdb/wlog/reader.go** - Sequential segment reading
- **tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go** - Live tailing of active segments
- **tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go** - Checkpoint creation for truncating old data
- **tsdb/wlog/watcher.go** - WAL monitoring and record processing

### Record Encoding:
- **tsdb/record/record.go** - Encoder/Decoder for all record types (series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, histograms, metadata)

### Integration Files:
- **tsdb/head_wal.go** - WAL integration with in-memory head block
- **tsdb/head_append.go** - WAL record writing during appends
- **tsdb/db.go** - Database-level WAL management
- **tsdb/agent/db.go** - Agent-specific WAL implementation

The answer includes detailed descriptions of key functions and symbols for:
- Segment creation and rotation (CreateSegment, NextSegment)
- Record encoding (Series, Samples, Tombstones, Exemplars, etc.)
- Corruption repair (Repair method)
- Checkpoint creation (Checkpoint, LastCheckpoint, DeleteCheckpoints)
- WAL reading and monitoring (Reader, LiveReader, Watcher)

\"symbol\": \"Metadata\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Prometheus TSDB write-ahead log (WAL) implementation is located in the tsdb/wlog package and related files. Here is a comprehensive overview of the implementation:\\n\\n## WAL Segment Creation and Rotation\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** contains the core WAL implementation:\\n- **CreateSegment()** and **OpenWriteSegment()** create and open new WAL segments\\n- **NextSegment()** and **NextSegmentSync()** manage segment rotation by creating a new segment when the current one is full, then asynchronously or synchronously closing the previous segment\\n- **Segment struct** represents a single WAL segment file with methods for writing and syncing\\n- **WL struct** is the main write-ahead log manager that tracks the active segment, manages paging (32KB pages), and handles compression\\n- **Log()** method writes records to the WAL, automatically triggering segment rotation when records are too large to fit in the remaining space\\n- **Segments()** and **listSegments()** enumerate all WAL segments and maintain sequential ordering\\n- **LastSegmentAndOffset()** returns the last segment number and the offset position within it\\n\\n## WAL Record Encoding\\n\\n**tsdb/record/record.go** implements record encoding/decoding for the WAL:\\n- **Encoder struct** with methods:\\n  - **Series()** encodes series records (metric labels with unique IDs)\\n  - **Samples()** encodes float sample records (timestamp-value pairs indexed by series ref)\\n  - **Tombstones()** encodes deletion records for deleted series\\n  - **Exemplars()** encodes exemplar records with labels\\n  - **HistogramSamples()** encodes classic histogram samples\\n  - **FloatHistogramSamples()** encodes native float histogram samples\\n  - **CustomBucketsHistogramSamples()** and **CustomBucketsFloatHistogramSamples()** for histograms with custom buckets\\n  - **MmapMarkers()** encodes memory-mapped chunk markers for out-of-order data\\n  - **Metadata()** encodes metric metadata (type, unit, help text)\\n- **Decoder struct** with methods to decode each record type from bytes\\n- **RefSeries, RefSample, RefTombstone, RefExemplar** structs hold encoded record data\\n- Records are delta-encoded for compression (timestamps and refs stored as deltas from the first record)\\n\\n## WAL Reading\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/reader.go** provides sequential reading of WAL segments:\\n- **Reader** reads WAL records from segment files\\n- **NewReader()** creates a reader for a set of segments\\n- Handles record fragments that span page boundaries\\n- Detects corruption and returns **CorruptionErr** with segment and offset information\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/live_reader.go** provides live tailing of actively-written WAL segments:\\n- **LiveReader** reads from an io.Reader (e.g., a segment being actively written)\\n- **NewLiveReader()** creates a live reader for real-time WAL monitoring\\n- Useful for remote write to tail WAL data as it's being written\\n- Handles EOF gracefully to allow waiting for more data\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/watcher.go** monitors WAL segments and processes records:\\n- **Watcher** watches the WAL directory for new segments and sends records to a WriteTo sink\\n- Used by remote write to consume WAL records\\n- Processes series, samples, exemplars, and metadata records\\n- Provides metrics for record reading progress\\n\\n## WAL Repair\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/wlog.go** includes corruption repair:\\n- **Repair()** method handles WAL corruption by:\\n  1. Taking a **CorruptionErr** that specifies the segment and byte offset of corruption\\n  2. Deleting all segments after the corrupted one\\n  3. Rewriting the corrupted segment, removing all records after the corruption point\\n  4. Creating a new segment to continue writing\\n- This discards corrupted data but preserves all valid records up to the corruption\\n\\n## Checkpoint Creation\\n\\n**tsdb/wlog/checkpoint.go** implements checkpoint creation to truncate old WAL data:\\n- **Checkpoint()** function creates a compacted checkpoint of WAL segments in a given range [from, to]\\n- **CheckpointStats** tracks how many series, samples, tombstones, exemplars, and metadata records were kept vs dropped\\n- **LastCheckpoint()** finds the most recent checkpoint directory and index\\n- **DeleteCheckpoints()** deletes old checkpoints below a given index\\n- **DeleteTempCheckpoints()** cleans up incomplete checkpoint directories\\n- Checkpoints are stored in directories named checkpoint.N (e.g., checkpoint.5) with the same segmented format as the WAL\\n- Allows filtering of series to keep via a keep() callback function\\n- Only includes data newer than a specified mint (minimum timestamp)\\n- This enables discarding old WAL files that are no longer needed, reducing storage requirements\\n\\n## Integration with Head Block\\n\\n**tsdb/head_wal.go** and **tsdb/head_append.go** integrate WAL with the in-memory head block:\\n- WAL replay on startup to reconstruct in-memory state\\n- Recording of series, samples, tombstones when they are added\\n- Tracking of WAL expiries for deleted series\\n\\n**tsdb/db.go** integrates WAL at the database level:\\n- Creates and manages the WAL instance\\n- Handles WAL replay and repair on startup\\n- Triggers checkpoint creation during compaction\\n- Manages WAL truncation when blocks are compacted\\n\\n**tsdb/agent/db.go** provides an agent-specific WAL implementation for remote-write use cases:\\n- Customized WAL that removes data immediately after remote write\\n- Repair and checkpoint functionality specific to agent mode\\n\\nAll these components work together to provide durable, recoverable storage of recent metrics data in the TSDB.\"\n}\n",
